=100  \\$aRameau, Jean-Philippe$d1683-1764$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1145$94787
=245  \\$aDardanus, tragédie
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bBallard$c1739
=300  \\$axxxiii-178 pages$boblong, leather bound embossed in gold, marbled endpapers
=500  \\$aDardanus is a tragédie en musique in a prologue and five acts. It premiered at the Paris Opéra on 19 November 1739 to mixed success, mainly because of the dramatic weakness of the libretto. This caused Rameau and La Bruère to rework the opera, completely rewriting the last three acts, for a revival in 1744. Only when Dardanus was again performed in 1760 did it win acclaim as one of Rameau's greatest works.

=100  \\$aWinter, Peter von$d1754-1825$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q561047$98194
=245  \\$aDer Zauberflöte zweiter Theil: $bDas Labyrinth oder der Kampf mit den Elementen
=260  \\$aBonn$bSimrock$c1799
=300  \\$a201-[1] pages
=500  \\$a'Das Labyrinth oder Der Kampf mit den Elementen. Der Zauberflöte zweyter Theil' is a "grand heroic-comic opera" in two acts composed in 1798 by Peter von Winter to a German libretto by Emanuel Schikaneder. The work is in the form of a Singspiel, a popular form that included both singing and spoken dialogue. The opera is a sequel of Mozart's The Magic Flute.

=041  \\$ager
=059  \\$av kbd
=100  \\$aDittersdorf, Karl Ditters von$d1739-1799$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q78522$97659
=245  \\$aQuintett Andante Grazioso.$bAria from Doctor und Apotheker: O wie herrlich, o wie labend
=260  \\$as.l.$c1786 or later
=300  \\$a11 pages
=500  \\$aTwo pieces in different handwritings; torn manuscript
=500  \\$aAct 1, Scene 1. 

Hauptmann Sturmwald mit einem Stelzfuß und einer Binde vor dem Auge; Apotheker Stößel mit einer langen Tabakspfeife, seine Frau Claudia, seine Nichte Rosalie und seine Tochter Leonore sitzen in der Laube, die Frauen mit Handarbeiten beschäftigt.

ALLE FÜNF.
O wie herrlich, o wie labend
Ist auf einen heißen Tag
So ein schöner kühler Abend,
Wo man sich erholen mag.
ROSALIE UND LEONORE für sich.
Noch weit schöner wär' der Abend,
Könnte Arm in Arm allein
Mein Geliebter bei mir sein.
STURMWALD für sich.
O wie köstlich, wie erlabend
Müßte jetzt ein gut Glas Wein
Für Verstand und Lunge sein!
ALLE FÜNF.
Welche angenehme Zeit!
STÖßEL UND CLAUDIA.
Denk' ich meiner jungen Jahre,
Denk' ich mir so manche Nacht,
Die ich göttlich hingebracht!
ALLE FÜNF.
O wie herrlich, o wie labend
Ist auf einen heißen Tag
So ein schöner kühler Abend,
Wo man sich erholen mag. 
Unvergleichlich, herzerquickend
Ist so eine Sommernacht.
Frohen Mutes und entzückend
Wird sie gerne durchgewacht!

=245  \\$aSongs$bpublished by G. Willig
=260  \\$aPhiladelphia$bWillig$c18xx
=300  \\$a8 pages$bprinted single sided, bound together with a piece of string
=500  \\$a6 American songs printed single sided, probably to sell as sets of two pages. 
=500  \\$aWith the song 'The stream let that flow'd round her cot' is printed that it is from the opera The Woodman. 
=500  \\$aUnder the score of the song 'Evening' is printed: I. Burger Sc.t. No 207 Queen Str.
And under the extra flute or guitar part: C. Tiebout Sculp. N.Y.
=500  \\$ahttps://librarycompany.org/research/subject-guides/music/ :
"In the 19th century, the development of lithography facilitated the production of affordable printed music. Philadelphia became a center for both music publishing and lithography, and the illustrated covers often depicted buildings, famous individuals, and sentimental genre scenes. Retailers such as George Willig, Alexander Fiot, and the firm Lee & Walker sold sheet music for both European and American tunes. Young women in middle- and upper-class households often demonstrated their accomplishments by playing the pianoforte. In general, music became part of a well-rounded education, and singing and playing music at home became a standard source of entertainment."
"The proliferation of cheap editions of classical and operatic works arranged for the piano demonstrates the democratization of high culture. Typically, Americans might attend a performance in a concert hall (symphonic, operatic, and ballet performances were common) and then purchase piano reductions for home use."

=100  \\$aCimarosa, Domenico$d1749-1801$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q191775$95848
=245  \\$aOrazi, ed i Curiazi. Opera seria ... aggiustata per il piano-forte
=260  \\$aBonn$bSimrock$cs.d. [1806?]
=300  \\$a86 pages$bcardboard bound marbled, leather spine and corners; cover and spine gild embossed, marbled endpapers$coblong
=500  \\$aOpera (azione tragica) in three acts based on Pierre Corneille's tragedy Horace. 
=500  \\$aPremiered in Venice, 1796
=500  \\$aCimarosa's “Gli Orazi e i Curiazi” represents the climax of his search for a “new genre” in Italian operatic tragedy and, at the same time, the setting and basic lyrics are emblematic of the development of new vocal personalities and new theatrical roles found in new vocal styles, especially that of the dramatic penetrating contralto, Giuseppina Grassini, and that of the new young heroic tenor, Matteo Babbini. The work was a huge and  long-lasting success.

=260  \\$aLeipzig$bBreitkopf & Härtel$cs.d. [1803]

=490  \\$aŒuvres complettes de Joseph Haydn$vCahier IX
=500  \\$aBeautiful title-page
=500  \\$aThe volume opens with a table of contents given the name and first line of each song in all languages used for each entry. Though the cover of this volume is in French, the title page gives the same information in German. This latter language also receives pride of place in the text underlay: Most songs are solely in German but, when lyrics are given in two languages, German is immediately below the musical staves with either Italian or French in italics below the German. Songs use one to three voices with the voice part sometimes integrated into the top staff of the piano part with text underlay indicating when to sing. Several songs are set for three-part Männerchor or four-part chorus with piano accompaniment. In strophic settings, only the first stanza of poetry appears in the score; the rest are included as addenda at the end of the piece.

=500  \\$aBeautiful print
=500  \\$aBologna-born Pietro Gaetano Boni settled in Rome in 1711 and served as ‘cello virtuoso’ to Corelli’s patron Cardinal Pietro Ottoboni, to whom his twelve Sonate per camera a violoncello e cembalo op.1 (Rome, 1717) were dedicated. He has long been forgotten along with his compositions and technical achievements on his instrument. 
In 1717, perhaps as a result of the publication of his op.1, he was made a member of the Accademia Filarmonica, Bologna. On the title-page of his Divertimenti Op.2 he is described as a priest.
=500  \\$aDedicatee was probably Don Marino Caracciolo VI (* 22-2-1696 + 1-7-1745). The House of Caracciolo is a prominent aristocratic family originating from the ancient kingdom of Naples, the first traces of which date back to the 10th century. The Caracciolos are considered one of the most important families in the history of the Kingdom of Naples, and also held relevant posts in the Spanish Empire.

=100  \\$aHiller, Johann Adam$d1728-1804$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q432299$95155
=245  \\$aLieder mit Melodien
=250  \\$a2nd rev. ed.
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bJunius$c1772
=300  \\$a[iv]-61-[1] pages$bcardboard binding, leather gold embossed spine and corners, marbled endpapers, engraved title page$coblong
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1760. Nos.1-14 were first published in 1759 
=500  \\$aJohann Adam Hiller was a German composer, conductor and writer on music, regarded as the creator of the Singspiel, an early form of German opera. In many of these operas he collaborated with the poet Christian Felix Weiße. Furthermore, Hiller was a teacher who encouraged musical education for women. He was Kapellmeister of Abel Seyler's theatrical company, and became the first Kapellmeister of Leipzig Gewandhaus. 
=500  \\$aRegister of names of all the poets included (Christian Felix Weisse (1726-1804) , Anna Luise Karsch (1722-1791) ,  Johann Timotheus Hermes (1738-1821) , Johann Wilhelm Ludwig Gleim (1719-1803) , Müller, Johann Georg Jacobi (1740-1814) , Kretschmann, Friedrich Wilhelm Gotter (1746-1797), Johann Peter Uz (1720-1796) and Fuchs.

=500  \\$aThe eight collections of Nouvelles poésies spirituelles et morales were published in Paris by Guillaume Desprez, Jean Desessartz, Philippe-Nicolas Lottin and Guichard from 1730 to 1737. This collection of more than four hundred spiritual parodies in French for voice and continuo, borrowed from seventy composers, was a great success in the 18th century, as shown by the reprints that were made.
=500  \\$aon music by Lully, Destouches, Desmarets, Clerambault, Bernier, Lambert, Beaupré, Gillier, Campra, Bertin, Marchand, Couperin, Marais, Debousset and others

=500  \\$aContains: 
- an explanation of the engraved titlepage, 
- a preface by the publisher on the use of this book,
- a preface by the composer which is also an introduction to playing basso continuo, chords, keys, preludia, ornaments, etc, followed by 
- six pages (Tab. I-VI) of musical examples to clarify this introduction.
- 150 Psalms (melody + figured bass in score)
- 12 other liturgical songs in similar fashion
=500  \\$aEach of the Psalms consists of one engraved page of music. The melodies have indications of trills and ornaments, text in an italic letter. The bass is figured and has the text in a roman letter. Below the score is listed how many verses there are, and also 'Pauze' and 'Stem ...'
=500  \\$aThe six pages of music that belong to the Preface contain interesting examples of ornaments (written out), the practice of playing/improvising between the lines of the Psalms, etc.

=500  \\$aNicolaas Simon van Winter (1718-1795) was, besides playwright and poet, salesman in pigments.
=500  \\$aContains a touching autograph dedication by the author to a granddaughter by law: Cornelia Christina van Orsoy, dating from his last years (and indeed clearly written by an elderly person). 
=500  \\$aCornelia Christina van Orsoy was a daughter of Anna Louisa van der Poorten (1742-1800), who married Pieter van Winter in 1780, thus becominging part of the Van Winter family.  
Pieter van Winter was the son of Nicolaas Simon van Winter and his first wife Johanna Muhl. After Johanna's death Nicolaas had married poet Lucretia van Merken, the couple had later moved from Amsterdam to Leiden. Apperently Lucretia had been fond of Cornelia and had wanted to give her this book. 
=500  \\$aDe Amstelstroom is an ode to the river Amstel.
=500  \\$aContains an engraved frontispiece, (with explanation), engraving on titlepage and a beautiful fold-out map of the Amstel (Pieter Meijer 1755).

Leyden, den 19 APril 1791, Nicolaas Simon van Winter"

=245  \\$aSumma totius theologiæ
=260  \\$aAntwerp$bPlantin$c1569
=300  \\$a[x]-[228]-374-[i]-[x]-376 pages$bbound in vellum
=500  \\$aOriginally 'Summa theologica', written 1265-74
=500  \\$aThe Summa Theologiae or Summa Theologica (transl. 'Summary of Theology'), often referred to simply as the Summa, is the best-known work of Thomas Aquinas, a scholastic theologian and Doctor of the Church. It is a compendium of all of the main theological teachings of the Catholic Church, intended to be an instructional guide for theology students, including seminarians and the literate laity. Presenting the reasoning for almost all points of Christian theology in the West, topics of the Summa follow the following cycle: God; Creation, Man; Man's purpose; Christ; the Sacraments; and back to God.
Although unfinished, it is "one of the classics of the history of philosophy and one of the most influential works of Western literature.

=500  \\$acontains score of Gerberts (?) 'Missa in coena domini' for double chorus and basso continuo
=500  \\$aBeautifully illustrated with wonderful engraved initial letters and an abundance of tables and illustrations of instruments and musical notations
=500  \\$aMartin Gerbert von Hornau was prince abbot at St Blaise Abbey in the Holy Roman Empire, mainly interested in sacramental theology, liturgiology, and notably ecclesiastical music. He was an outstanding music historian and a representative of the modern Benedictine order in the Black Forest (Baden-Württemberg Germany). The materials for his work he had gathered during his travels, and although it contains many textual errors, its publication has been of great importance for the history of music, by preserving writings which might either have perished or remained unknown. His interest in music led to his acquaintance with the composer Gluck, who became his intimate friend.

=041  \\$adut
=245  \\$aStichtelyke gedichten
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bYntema$bTieboel$c1775
=300  \\$a[iv]-xii-[14]-420-[31] pages$bengraved title page, leather spine and corners, marbled cardboard cover
=500  \\$aIn 1770, Agatha Deken became the paid 'compagne' and soon 'soul friend' of a sickly young woman, Maria Bosch, in Amsterdam. During this period, she began to write. Deken made her debut in the Hedendaagsche Vaderlandsche Letteroefeningen in 1772 with the poem 'Euzebia or the godly maidservant'. Other poems show that she kept in touch with the orphanage where she was raised. In 1773, Maria Bosch died. Two years later, a collection of Stichtelyke gedichten by Agatha Deken and Maria Bosch appeared, generously published with a title engraving by Reinier Vinkeles, possibly paid for by Maria Bosch's mother, possibly also by Deken's wealthy cousin Hendrik Busserus (patron of Vinkeles), to whom the book was dedicated and who later left her an inheritance of over thirteen thousand guilders. Deken supplied most of the collected verses. The book shows something of a small circle of friends, or a poetry society, in which piety is the main binding element. We meet in the volume, among others, a friend of Deken's, Maria Elizabeth Schreuder, with whom she conducted a pious-introspective correspondence. She probably supported herself with a tea business during these years.

=245  \\$aRegina Cœli
=260  \\$aUtrecht$bRoothaan$c1869
=300  \\$a[ii]-40-4-4-4-4-19 pages$bpaper binding, loose vocal parts
=490  \\$aVereeniging voor Nederlandsche Muziekgeschiedenis. Uitgave van oudere Noord-nederlandsche meesterwerken$vI
=500  \\$acontains a Dutch biography of Sweelinck by H. Tiedeman, and an extensive bliography with commentary (both translated in reduced form in German by Emil Mohr)
=500  \\$acontains the vocal parts as well as a pianoscore
=500  \\$aFirst published in Cantiones sacrae (no. 33) in Antwerp,1619 
=500  \\$aThe Regina Cæli or Regina Cœli “Queen of Heaven”, is an ancient Latin Marian Hymn of the Christian Church. It is one of the four seasonal Marian antiphons of the Blessed Virgin Mary, prescribed to be sung or recited in the Liturgy of the Hours at the conclusion of the last of the hours to be prayed in common that day, typically night prayer (Compline or Vespers).   Anyone of these four or of other suitable antiphons may now be sung at any time of the liturgical year.   The Regina Coeli is sung or recited in place of the Angelus during the Easter season, from Easter Sunday until Pentecost.

=041  \\$adut
=245  \\$aBeknopte beschrijving der hedendaagsche pianino
=250  \\$a3rd ed.
=260  \\$aRotterdam$bRijken & de Lange$c1920
=300  \\$a24-[2] pages$bpaper bound, front-and backcover in black and red ink, photos, musical examples, illustrations
=500  \\$apiano trade and grand piano building 'Rijken and De Lange' Rotterdam 1852-1981
=500  \\$aThe Rijken & De Lange firm was founded in Rotterdam in 1852. Initially, Georg and Jan Rijken, brothers and founders, had no other business capital than a large dose of professional knowledge, a lot of zest for work and each a beautiful tenor voice, with which they made many friends, especially among musicians. Together with Samuel de Lange, organist and well-known tone artist providing start-up capital and accommodation, among other things, they laid the foundations for a company that soon found itself at the centre of Rotterdam's musical life.
At the beginning of the 20th century, the firm Rijken & De Lange published a booklet, which was free for the benefit of all future pianists. The booklet clearly covered the construction of the piano and grand piano.

=100  \\$aDoorslaer, Georges van$c1864-1940$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q55683472$4aut$96644
=245  \\$aLa Vie et les œuvres de Philippe de Monte
=260  \\$aBrussels$bLamertin$bHayez$c1921
=300  \\$a309-[1] pages
=490  \\$aAcadémie royale de Belgique, classe des beaux-arts, mémoires, Collection in-8°$vtome 1, fascicule IV et dernier
=520  \\$aVan Doorslaer, a Belgian musicologist, was president of the Cercle archéologique de Malines and a member of the Académie royale d'archéologie de Belgique. A physician by profession, he studied music as a vocation. He wrote valuable essays such as 'Kerry Bredemers, 1472-1522' (Antwerp, 1915), 'De Toonkunstenaars der familie Vredeman' (Antwerp, 1920), 'La Vie et les œuvres de Philippe de Monte' (Brussels, 1921), and 'Rinaldo del Mel' (Antwerp, 1922). He also edited eight volumes in the collected edition of works by Philippe de Monte.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aBonneval, Michel de$d? - 1766$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3311139$4aut$96652
=245  \\$aLes Romans. $bBallet héroïque
=260  \\$aParis$bBallard$c1736
=300  \\$aviii-65-[1] pages$bmarbled paper cover,  engraved title page
=500  \\$aAs general controller of the silverware and intendant of the king's Menus-Plaisirs, Bonneval - choreographer, librettist and production dramatist - was responsible for spending on clothes and furniture, and for organising balls, fêtes, masquerades, carousels, etc. He composed many of the operas performed at court, on the Versailles stage.
=500  \\$aFirst performed in 1736, music by Jean-Baptiste Niel (1690 – 1775) Master of music and batteur de mesure at the Opéra. In 1736 he secured a licence to write keyboard works, which have now disappeared. He performed with some success at the Concert-Spirituel, but he was most famous for composing opera-ballets or heroic ballets such as Les Romans (1736, lyrics by Bonneval) or L'École des amants (1744). The former was a great success, and was performed at court in front of the Queen in 1737. The music, however, was not very personal, and borrowings from Rameau were notable. We have a score in which the composer explains that he has introduced a new accent on the e, between the silent e and the open e, as well as new signs for the figured bass.
=534  \\$aPremiered at the Académie royale de musique on 23 August 1736

=500  \\$aMusic by Jean-Baptiste Lully, premiered in 1678
=500  \\$aPsyché is an opera (tragédie lyrique) in a prologue and five acts (libretto adapted from Molière's original play for which Lully had composed the intermèdes). Based on the love story of Cupid and Psyche, Psyché was premiered on April 19, 1678 by the Académie Royale de Musique at the Théâtre du Palais-Royal in Paris.

=260  \\$aLondon$bArnold$c1789

=490  \\$aThe Works of G. F. Händel, Ed. in Score$vplate nos. 49-54
=500  \\$aSamson (HWV 57) is a three-act oratorio by George Frideric Handel, considered one of his finest dramatic works. It is usually performed as an oratorio in concert form, but on occasions has also been staged as an opera. The well-known arias "Let the bright Seraphim" (for soprano), "Total eclipse" (for tenor) and "Let their celestial concerts" (the final chorus) are often performed separately in concert.
=500  \\$aIt uses a libretto by Newburgh Hamilton, who based it on John Milton's Samson Agonistes, which in turn was based on the figure Samson in Chapter 16 of the Book of Judges.

=500  \\$aThe Handel organ concertos, Op. 4, HWV 289–294, are six organ concertos for chamber organ and orchestra composed by George Frideric Handel in London between 1735 and 1736 and published in 1738 by the printing company of John Walsh. Written as interludes in performances of oratorios in Covent Garden, they were the first works of their kind for this combination of instruments and served as a model for later composers.

=245  \\$aGiulio Cesare, opera in tre atti rappresentata al teatro del Re nel Mercato del fieno a Londra nell'anno 1723
=260  \\$aLondon$bArnold$c1787-97
=300  \\$a170 pages
=490  \\$aThe Works of G. F. Händel, Ed. in Score$vplate nos. 43-47
=500  \\$a'Giulio Cesare in Egitto' (Julius Caesar in Egypt) is a dramma per musica (opera seria) in three acts composed by George Frideric Handel for the Royal Academy of Music in 1724. The libretto was written by Nicola Francesco Haym who used an earlier libretto by Giacomo Francesco Bussani, which had been set to music by Antonio Sartorio (1676). The opera was a success at its first performances, was frequently revived by Handel in his subsequent opera seasons and is now one of the most often performed Baroque operas.
=500  \\$aThe opera's plot is loosely based on historic events during the Roman Civil War of 49–45 BC.

=500  \\$aChristiaan Huygens, Lord of Zeelhem, (1629-1695) was a Dutch mathematician, physicist, engineer, astronomer, and inventor who is regarded as a key figure in the Scientific Revolution.
=500  \\$aHuygens preferred meantone temperament; he innovated in 31 equal temperament (which was not itself a new idea but known to Francisco de Salinas), using logarithms to investigate it further and show its close relation to the meantone system.

=100  \\$aBock, Gustav$d1813-1863$4edt$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q100533909$96657
=245  \\$aNeue Berliner Musikzeitung$nvol. 6
=260  \\$aBerlin$bBote & Bock$c1852
=300  \\$a400-4 pages
=500  \\$aIncomplete. nrs 1-2 missing.
=500  \\$aThe 'Neue Berliner Musikzeitung' ran from 1846 until 1896
=500  \\$aBock was the first son of the pedagogue Moses Hirsch Bock (1781-1816). He trained as a book, art and music dealer and in 1831 joined the "Buch- und Musikalien-Verlags- wie auch Sortimentshandlung" C.W. Froehlich & Comp, founded by Traugott Friedrich Julius Ahlemann. In 1842 he married Emilie Brody. The couple set up a musical salon in their private flat, where they held private concerts. Together with Eduard Bote, Bock founded the Musikverlag on 27 January 1838 by taking over the music shop C. W. Froehlich and founded the music publishing house Ed. Bote & G. Bock. Bock was one of the largest German music publishers and one of the best-known personalities in Berlin in the 1840s to 1860s.In 1845, together with others, Bock founded the Berliner Tonkünstlerverein and the Neue Berliner Musikzeitung.

=008  211119s1661\\\\\\\|||||\||||\00|\p\fre\d
=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aBacilly, Bertrand de$dc. 1625-1690$4aut$4col$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2899715$96686
=245  \\$aRecueil des plus beaux vers qui ont esté mis en chant
=260  \\$aParis$bSercy, de$c1661
=300  \\$a[xxx]-536 pages$bengraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aFirst of ten such collections published between 1661 and 1680.
=500  \\$aOriginally dedicated to the superintendent Nicolas Fouquet; but after his disgrace, the dedication was quickly replaced by another to Paul Pellisson-Fontanier, Fouquet's secretary. 
=500  \\$aCollection compiled by Benigne de Bacilly, priest and composer, comprising 498 pieces of verse set to song, 277 of which are signed. Many of them appear here for the first time, including 18 by Benserade, 5 by Boisrobert, 68 by Bouillon, 12 by Pellisson, 9 by Scarro, and 5 by Segrais. The airs are by Le Camus, Lambert, Bacilly, Dassoucy, Batiste, Boesset, Moulinié etc. The poems are arranged in alphabetical order of the incipits.
=520  \\$aThe collections of "verses mis en chant" published by Bacilly constitute a very rich compilation of the airs that were sung in Paris in the 1660's. They constitute very interesting documentation because, although published without music, they mention both the name of the poet author of the verses and the name of the musician who set them to music. About ten of these collections were published between 1661 and 1671 by Charles de Sercy, Étienne Loyson, Guillaume de Luyne, Robert III Ballard or Bacilly himself.

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aContains 'Das Vorspiel , ein Satirische Episches Gedicht in fünf Büchern', a satirical-epic poem directed against Gottsched, originally published 1742, 
The volume also contains Rost's erotic-gallant poem "Der Brautnacht"(The Weddingnight)  (originally published as 'Die schöne Nacht' in 1754) one of those poems for which Rost was more notorious than famous and which "drove the fair blush of shame on virginal cheeks"
The two remaining poems, 'Der fröhliche Jüngling' and 'Die Nachtigall' , are not by Rost, but by J.Fr. Lamprecht and Chr. N. Neumann respectively.

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aMerken, Lucretia Wilhelmina van$d1721-1789$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3265974$95933
=245  \\$aJacob Simonszoon de Ryk. $bTreurspel
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bMeijer$c1774
=300  \\$a[iv]-87 pages
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aVery succesful play about an episode in the Eighty Years' War (or Dutch War of Independence, 1568–1648), first staged at the Schouwburg of Amsterdam.
=500  \\$aThe play is set in Gent, in the Castle of the Counts (Gravensteen)
=500  \\$aIn 1774, the poet Lucretia Wilhelmina van Merken published a sensational play: Jacob Simonszoon de Ryk. This tragedy revolves around the heroic deeds of the sixteenth-century 'Watergeus' (Sea Beggar) De Rijk, a rebel during the Eighty Years' War who fled and issued with a privateer's certificate was entitled to fight as a privateer for the Republic against the Spanish. He ends up in Spanish captivity and becomes the focus of complex diplomatic negotiations. Thanks to his courage and perseverance, he manages to escape together with his four fellow combatants.
=500  \\$aJacob Simonszoon de Ryk was first performed at the reopening of the Amsterdamse Schouwburg in 1774. The crowds were so large that soldiers had to be called in to keep them under control. The heroic episode from the Eighty Years' War was so popular that it was performed many more times. It was a box-office success.
=500  \\$a Van Merken was in her day considered one of the best writers in the Netherlands. Contemporaries praised her poetic talent and called her 'the miracle of Europe'. She can rightly be called the female Vondel of the eighteenth century.
=500  \\$aMissing: pages 1-2,47-50

=100  \\$aSinold von Schütz, Philipp Balthasar$d1657-1742$4edt$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q17130894$96734
=245  \\$aDie Europäische Fama,$bwelche den gegenwärtigen Zustand der vornehmsten Höfe entdecket.$nvols. 1 (Theil 1-8), 11 (Theil 121-132), 13 (Theil 145-155) and 15 (Theil 169-180)
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bGleditsch$c1702; 1711-16
=300  \\$a4 vols. ([iv]-772 + 618-[xvi]-433-[10] + 428-[viii]-605-[4] +564-[xvi]424-[25]) pages$billustrations, bound in white vellum
=500  \\$aVon Schütz was civil servant, publicist, writer and theologian, and finally privy councillor to the Count of Solms-Laubach. Returning home to Germany after a trip to Italy, he lived for several years in Leipzig as a private scholar and here published a journal, Die europäische Fama (1704), in which he examined politics from a Christian point of view.  Continuations of this journal by others appeared later as "Neue europäische Fama" (Leipzig 1735 ff.) and "Neueste europäische Fama" (Gotha 1760 ff.).
=500  \\$avol.11 contains an unpaginated book-catalogue of the editor Gleditsch of 16 pages between Theil 127 & 128
=500  \\$avol.13 contains an unpaginated book-catalogue of the editor Gleditsch of 8 pages between Theil 149 & 150
=500  \\$avol.15 contains an unpaginated book-catalogue of the editor Gleditsch of 16 pages between Theil 175 & 176
=500  \\$a3 vols. ex libris  Christian Ernst Graf zu Stolberg (1691-1771).The golden age of the Stolberg library was during the reign of Christian Ernst (1710-1771). He not only greatly increased its holdings and opened it to the public, but was also its librarian, commissioning the distinctive Stolberg bookplate and personally inscribing the publication date on the spine of each volume bound in white vellum. In 1746 Christian Ernst issued an edict making the collection—by then about 10,000 volumes—a public library.

=500  \\$aThe "Neue europäische Fama" (Leipzig 1735 ff.) and "Neueste europäische Fama" (Gotha 1760 ff.) were continuations of "Die europäische Fama" (1704), a series of periodic journals first published by Sinold von Schütz.

=500  \\$aex libris Christian Ernst Graf zu Stolberg (1691-1771).The golden age of the Stolberg library was during the reign of Christian Ernst (1710-1771). He not only greatly increased its holdings and opened it to the public, but was also its librarian, commissioning the distinctive Stolberg bookplate and personally inscribing the publication date on the spine of each volume bound in white vellum. In 1746 Christian Ernst issued an edict making the collection—by then about 10,000 volumes—a public library.

=100  \\$aRemond de Sainte-Albine, Pierre$d1699-1778$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3386898$96740
=245  \\$aLe Comédien
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bDesaint & Saillant$bVincent$c1747
=300  \\$a312-[5] pages$billustrations
=500  \\$aFrontispiece designed by Gravelot, with the motto “Facies mutat semperque decenter.”
=520  \\$a'Le Céomdien' is comprehensive work designed to lay down the principles of the profession for novice actors. The author's intention was, "while awaiting the publication of a treatise on the Art of Acting such as one would be entitled to desire, to help those who wish to embrace this Profession to know whether they are suitable for the Theatre, and to discover some of the means by which they can hope to win applause there". The author ends his speech with a declaration in favour of recognising young talent, and against "the sad folly of the admirers of the past". This treatise provoked Diderot's 'Paradoxe du comédien' (1770-8).

=041  \\$adut$alat
=245  \\$aBrief van Bernardus Forckenbeck aen Iacobum Omphalium; Brief van Bernardus Forckenbeck aen Henricum Welsingium; Brief van Jacobus Omphalius aen Aemilium Trebatium
=260  \\$aDeventer et al.$bs.n.$c1611
=300  \\$a32 pages
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aBernardus Forckenberg, together with Henricus Welsing and Jacobus Omphalius, commissioned the anonymous book 'Officio hominis Christini', which defended the doctrines of Socinianism and advised the reader to join the Polish Socinians without delay. Socinianism is a Non-trinitarian Christian belief system named after the Italian theologians Lelio Sozzini (Latin: Laelius Socinus) and Fausto Sozzini (Latin: Faustus Socinus), which was developed among the Polish Brethren in the Polish Reformed Church during the 16th and 17th centuries. The Socinian booklet, defending Conrad Vorstius (1569-1622) a German-Dutch heterodox Remonstrant theologian, caused an uproar in Friesland. Even before the Frisian justice system could arrest the perpetrators, the three Vorstius-adepts made their way to Steinfurt.

=100  \\$aBosch Kemper, Jeronimo de$d1808-1876$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2271540$96746
=245  \\$aDirk Rafaelsz Camphuizen, de vrije evangelie-belijder in het tijdvak van het kerkelijk gezang
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bWitkamp$c1872
=300  \\$a32 pages
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aDirk Rafelsz Camphuysen (1586-1627) was a Dutch painter, poet and theologian. Camphuysen left a translation of the Psalms, and a number of short pieces of poetry. He was also author of several theological works, among which is a Compendium Doctrinae Sociniorum. He was relatively successful as a minister, but he had embraced the doctrines of Arminianism, and like other Arminians or Remonstrants, he was banned from ministry and teaching and driven into exile (1619).The Remonstrants is a Protestant movement that had split from the Dutch Reformed Church in the early 17th century. The early Remonstrants supported Jacobus Arminius, and after his death, continued to maintain his original views called Arminianism against the proponents of Calvinism.

=500  \\$aSee X2B24 for 1718 edition (which is similar but has different illustrations)
=500  \\$aJohann Quirsfeld (1642-1686) was a composer and theologian who worked as Kantor of St Marien in Pirna near Dresden
=500  \\$aFrontispiece printed in red and black ink
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Geistreiches Gesang-Buch'
=563  \\$aBinding with metal clasps
=590  \\$aDarmit sich eine in Christo andächtige Seele zieren kan bey Morgens und Abends, und jeder Jahrs-Zeit für Frauen und Jungfrauen, hohen und niedrigen Standes, auf allerley dererselben eigentliche Zufälle auch bey Buß, Beicht u. h. Abendmahl, auf alle Fest- und Sonntage durchs gantze Jahr bey Trauren, Kranckheiten, Sterben und allerley Widerwärtigkeit. In Zwölfferley geistlichen Habit abgetheilet in einem Gebet- und Gesang-Buche, als einem geistl. Schmuck-Kästlein, mit zwölf unterschiedlichen Fächlein aus göttlichem Worte gezeiget und mit vier und zwanzig Kupfern gezieret

=245  \\$aMaandelyksche berichten uit de andere waerelt, July-December 1740
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bRatelband$c1740
=300  \\$a642-107-[8] pages$b5 plates inserted
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe 'Maandelyksche Berichten' are alternated with 'Staat nieuws' for every month
=500  \\$a"Het literaire genre van het dodengesprek (een fictief gesprek tussen twee of meer overledenen in het hiernamaals) is voor het eerst beoefend door de Grieks schrijvende Syriër Lucianus (120 – 180 na Chr.) Maar waar zijn Dodengesprekken een komisch en vooral satirisch karakter hadden, zijn de ‘Maandelyksche berichten’ hoofdzakelijk informatief van aard; ze geven stukken politieke geschiedenis en biografieën van de twee gesprekspartners. Ze zijn geschreven door de Duitser David Fassman en van 1718 tot 1739 in Leipzig uitgegeven. De Nederlandse vertalingen verschenen van 1721 tot en met 1754, en (samen met ander vertaald materiaal) van 1755 tot 1771, waarmee de ‘Maandelyksche berichten’ een van de langst verschenen Nederlandse tijdschriften van de achttiende eeuw zijn. Zie verder: Veenman, ‘Het dodengesprek in Nederland’, in: De Achttiende Eeuw 29 (1997)"

=500  \\$aThere also exists a fourth volume, see https://archive.org/details/mmoirescontenan00brangoog/page/n8
=500  \\$avol.3 = 09F22
=500  \\$aPierre de Bourdeille was a French historian, soldier and biographer.
=500  \\$aDe Bourdeille can hardly be regarded as a historian proper, and his Memoirs cannot be accepted as a very trustworthy source of information. But he writes in a quaint conversational way, pouring forth his thoughts, observations or facts without order or system, and with the greatest frankness.
His works give a picture of the general court-life of the time, with its unblushing and undisguised profligacy. There is not an homme illustre or a dame galante in all his gallery of portraits who has not engaged in sexual immorality; and yet the whole is narrated with the most complete unconsciousness that there is anything objectionable in their conduct.
[Chisholm, Hugh, ed. (1911). "Pierre de Bourdeille, Seigneur and Abbé de Brantôme". Encyclopædia Britannica. 4 (11th ed.). Cambridge University Press.]

=100  \\$aSecundus, Johannes$d1511-1536$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q614229$96787
=245  \\$aOpera accurato recognita ex Museo P. Scriverii
=260  \\$aLeiden$bHeger, de$c1631

=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$a Engraved title page with portrait medallion ("vatis amatoris iulia sculpta manu"); author's portrait on verso of tenth preliminary leaf. 
=500  \\$aJan Everaerts (Secundus) was a New Latin poet of Dutch nationality. He wrote elegies, epigrams, odes, epistles, epithalimia, itineraries, and other prose. His most famous work was Liber Basiorum (Book of Kisses) which is among the works in this volume (p.79-92) The compiler, Peter Schrijver (Scriverius) was was a Dutch antiquarian, philologist, writer and scholar on the history of Holland and Belgium.
=500  \\$aSecundus was a prolific writer, and in his short life he produced several books of elegies on his lovers Julia and Neaera, epigrams, odes, verse epistles and epithalamia, as well as some prose writings (epistles and itineraria).
His most famous work, though, was the Liber Basiorum (Book of Kisses, first complete edition 1541), a short collection consisting of nineteen poems in various metres, in which the poet explores the theme of the kiss in relation to his Spanish lover, Neaera.
=500  \\$aScriverius, was a profilic publisher of humanist literature. He collected manuscripts of Neolatine authors from his own time and from the time of early humanism. Based on these, he produced a number of editions, including the Latin poetry of Janus Secundus (first published in 1619).

=500  \\$aThe abbé Marc-Antoine Laugier was a Jesuit priest and architectural theorist. With the collaboration of the journalist and theatre historian Antoine de Léris and Antoine Jacques Labbet, abbé de Morambert, he edited this journal, which only appeared in two issues. It was the first in France to be specifically devoted to music.

=100  \\$aHomeros$d9th Century BC-8th Century BC$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q6691$94802
=245  \\$aOdyssea Batrachomyomachia, Hymni & epigrammata græce et latine
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bWettstein$c1743
=300  \\$a579-[19] pages$btitle page in red and black ink, folded sheet inserted
=500  \\$aThe Odyssey is one of the oldest extant works of literature still widely read by modern audiences. As with the Iliad, the poem is divided into 24 books.
=500  \\$aThe epic poem was, as the Odyssey, likely written down in Homeric Greek, a literary amalgam of Ionic Greek and other dialects, probably around the late 8th or early 7th century BC. By the mid-6th century BCE, had become part of the Greek literary canon.
=500  \\$aCrucial themes in the poem include the ideas of nostos ("return"), wandering, xenia ("guest-friendship"), testing, and omens. Scholars still reflect on the narrative significance of certain groups in the poem, such as women and slaves, who have a more prominent role in the epic than in many other works of ancient literature. This focus is especially remarkable when contrasted with the Iliad, which centres the exploits of soldiers and kings during the Trojan War. 
=500  \\$aSamuel Clarke (1675-1729) was an English philosopher and Anglican cleric. He is considered the major British figure in philosophy between John Locke and George Berkeley.
=520  \\$aThe Odyssey follows the Greek hero Odysseus, king of Ithaca, and his journey home after the Trojan War. After the war, which lasted ten years, his journey lasted for ten additional years, during which time he encountered many perils and all his crew mates were killed. In his absence, Odysseus was assumed dead, and his wife Penelope and son Telemachus had to contend with a group of unruly suitors who were competing for Penelope's hand in marriage.
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1740
=648  \0$aClassical Antiquity (8th Century BC-6th Century AD)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q486761$921435

=041  \\$agre$alat$hgrc
=100  \\$aHomeros$d9th Century BC-8th Century BC$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q6691$94802
=245  \\$aIlias, Græce et Latine
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bWettstein$c1743
=300  \\$a[ii]-619-[9] pages$btitle page in red and black ink, engraved frontispiece, folded sheet inserted
=500  \\$aThe Iliad is one of the oldest extant works of literature still widely read by modern audiences. As with the Odyssey, the poem is divided into 24 books and contains 15,693 lines in its most widely accepted version, and was written in dactylic hexameter. The Iliad is often regarded as the first substantial piece of European literature.
=500  \\$aThe Iliad, as the Odyssey, were likely written down in Homeric Greek, a literary amalgam of Ionic Greek and other dialects, probably around the late 8th or early 7th century BC.
=500  \\$aCritical themes in the poem include kleos (glory), pride, fate and wrath. The poem is frequently described as a masculine or heroic epic, especially compared with the Odyssey. It contains detailed descriptions of ancient war instruments and battle tactics, and fewer female characters. The Olympian gods also play a major role in the poem, aiding their favoured warriors on the battlefield and intervening in personal disputes. Their characterisation in the poem humanised them for Ancient Greek audiences, giving a concrete sense of their cultural and religious tradition. In terms of formal style, the poem's repetitions, use of similes and epithets, are often explored by scholars.
=500  \\$aSamuel Clarke (1675-1729) was an English philosopher and Anglican cleric. He is considered the major British figure in philosophy between John Locke and George Berkeley.
=520  \\$aSet towards the end of the Trojan War, a ten-year siege of the city of Troy by a coalition of Mycenaean Greek states, the poem depicts significant events in the siege's final weeks. In particular, it depicts a fierce quarrel between King Agamemnon and a celebrated warrior, Achilles. It is a central part of the Epic Cycle.

=500  \\$aAlain-René Lesage (1668-1747) was a French novelist and playwright. Lesage is best known for his comic novel The Devil upon Two Sticks (1707, Le Diable boiteux), his comedy Turcaret (1709), and his picaresque novel Gil Blas (1715–1735). Le Bachelier de Salamanque is the last novel by Lesage.

=100  \\$aSweerts, Hieronymous$d1629-1696$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2693785$96820
=245  \\$aDe tien vermakelikheden des houwelyks
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bSweerts$c1678
=300  \\$a172 pages$billustrations, frontispiece engraving, bound in white velum
=500  \\$aBound in with other writings about marriage
=500  \\$aHieronymus Sweerts was an art dealer, print publisher, bookseller, poet and  author who also published under the pseudonym Jeroen Jeroense or under Hippolytus de Vrye. He wrote a large number of (often witty or farcical) poems (together some 900 pages) and a number of other works. Some individual poems appeared in print during his lifetime. After his death, his son Cornelis Sweerts collected and published his poems under the title Alle de gedichten (1697). Sweerts moved in the literary circle that opposed the strict-classicist views of the Amsterdam art society Nil Volentibus Arduum.

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aAphthonius of Antioch$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q4441106$96823
=245  \\$aProgymnasmata
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bElsevier$c1649
=300  \\$a441-[14] pages$bengraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aProgymnasmata are a series of preliminary rhetorical exercises that began in ancient Greece and continued during the Roman Empire. These exercises were implemented by students of rhetoric, who began their schooling between ages twelve and fifteen. The purpose of these exercises was to prepare students for writing declamations after they had completed their education with the grammarians. There are only four surviving handbooks of progymnasmata, attributed to Aelius Theon, Hermogenes of Tarsus, Aphthonius of Antioch, and Nicolaus the Sophist.
=500  \\$aAphthonius of Antioch was a student of the great sophist Libanius during the second half of the fourth century. This is the most widely used and referenced handbook that became the standard on the practice of progymnasmata. His treatises were combined with rhetorical treatises of Hermogenes on stasis theory and style to create the “Hermogenic Corpus.” 
=500  \\$aIn Aphthonius Progymnasmata, all students were asked to write out each assignment, memorize it, and then perform a class oration. The progymnasmata were taught in order, increasing in difficulty as the course advances. The courses were organized to begin with story-telling and end with making an argument. There was a focus on literature as a supplement to the course, paying close attention to models of rhetoric and literature. The progymnasmata of Aphthonius was first translated to Latin in the fifteenth century by Rudolphus Agricola.

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aSallustius$d86 BC-c. 35 BC$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7170$95745
=245  \\$aDe L. Sergii Catilinæ coniuratione, ac Bello Iugurthino historiæ
=260  \\$aLeiden$bVincentius$c1556
=300  \\$a263-[45] pages$bbound in white velum, oversized bowed cover, manuscript annotations
=500  \\$a"On the conspiracy of L. Sergius Catiline, and the history of the Jugurthine war. With some others, which the following page will tell."
=500  \\$aLucius Sergius Catilina was a Roman politician and soldier. He is best known for instigating the Catilinarian conspiracy, a failed attempt to violently seize control of the Roman state in 63 BC. 
=500  \\$aDe bello Iugurthino (also: Bellum Iugurthinum) is Sallust's second historical monograph after De coniuratione Catilinae. The work deals with the events of the war waged by Gaius Marius and Lucius Cornelius Sulla Felix in 111-106 BC against the Numidian king Jugurtha and was written around 40 BC. The main theme of the work is not so much the description of the Jugurthine War, but rather the presentation of certain internal political conditions in Rome. Above all, the contrast between the nobility and the plebeians, the unpleasantness of party fights and the civil wars are discussed. At the end of his explanations, Sallust puts forward the thesis that the decline of the commonwealth was due to the politicians' striving for power.

=100  \\$aMartialis, Marcus Valerius$d40-104$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2098$95051
=245  \\$aEpigrammaton $blibri 14
=260  \\$aParis$bColinæus$c1544

=500  \\$aMarcus Valerius Martialis was a Roman poet from Hispania (modern Spain) best known for his twelve books of Epigrams, published in Rome between AD 86 and 103, during the reigns of the emperors Domitian, Nerva and Trajan. In these short, witty poems he cheerfully satirises city life and the scandalous activities of his acquaintances, and romanticises his provincial upbringing. He wrote a total of 1,561 epigrams, of which 1,235 are in elegiac couplets. Martial has been called the greatest Latin epigrammatist and is considered the creator of the modern epigram.

=100  \\$aRosa, Salvator$d1615-1673$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q359421$96831
=245  \\$aSatire ... dedicate a Settano
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bProthomastix$c1694 [?]
=300  \\$a160-[1] pages$bcoloured gilded enpapers, leather bound, embossed gilded spine
=500  \\$aSalvator Rosa is best known today as an Italian Baroque painter, whose romanticized landscapes and history paintings, often set in dark and untamed nature, exerted considerable influence from the 17th century into the early 19th century. In his lifetime he was among the most famous painters, known for his flamboyant personality, and regarded as an accomplished poet, satirist, actor, musician, and printmaker, as well. He was active in Naples, Rome, and Florence, where on occasion he was compelled to move between cities, as his caustic satire earned him enemies in the artistic and intellectual circles of the day.
=500  \\$aOriginally published in Venice, 1658
=500  \\$apirate edition of a forbidden work (see note on fs: "Proibito")

=500  \\$athe first satire deals with 'La musica' (pages 5-25), the following ones with 'La poesia', 'La pittura', 'La guerra', 'La Babilonia', 'L'Invidia', all writen in tercets (see Dante)
=500  \\$aQuinto Settano was the ps. of the poet Lodovico Sergardi (1660-1726), whose own satires were only published in 1694
=500  \\$aThe six satires by the Neapolitan painter and man of letters constitute as many witty invectives against the vices of the century (Music. Poetry, Painting, War, Babylon, Envy). Confused, disoriented, illogical, he jumps from one thing to another, he says and says again; his thought seems poorly formed and elaborated. What Rosa never lacks is the eagerness, the violence, the loquacity, proper to his character .

=100  \\$aMouret, Jean-Joseph$d1682-1738$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q960766$96839
=245  \\$aLes Amours des Dieux. $bBallet héroïque
=260  \\$aParis$bMourette$bBoivin$bLe Clerc$c1730
=300  \\$a[ii]-3-[i]-41-47-87-75-60 pages
=500  \\$aCondensed score
=500  \\$aThe various segments are paginated separately
=505  \\$gPrologue -- Neptune et Amymone -- Jupiter et Niobé -- Apollon et Coronis -- Arianne et Bachus
=520  \\$aMouret’s Les amours des dieux is classified as a ballet-heroïque, a type of opéra-ballet that was popular during the first half of the eighteenth century. Although the term ballet-heroïque suggests the prevalence of dance, drawing on the divertissement tradition, singing and acting are also integral parts of this genre. What distinguishes the opéra-ballet from the tragedie en musique is the use of separate plots for each entrée (comparable to an act). The segments are not entirely independent, however, in that there is typically a central, overarching idea.
=534  \\$aFirst performed at the Académie Royale de Musique, Paris, 1727

=100  \\$aHiller, Johann Adam$d1728-1804$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q432299$95155
=245  \\$aDie Jagd.$bEine comische Oper in drey Acten
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bBreitkopf$c1771
=300  \\$a101-[1] pages$bengraved title page
=500  \\$a'Die Jagd' is considered one of the most important early Singspiele. It was admired by Goethe and Wagner..The libretto is based on the plays La partie de chasse de Henri IV by Charles Collé, The King and the Miller of Mansfield by Robert Dodsley, and the opéra comique by Michel-Jean Sedaine (originally set by Monsigny). 
=534  \\$aThe opera was first performed at the Schlosstheater, Weimar, on 29 January 1770. 
=561  \\$aEx Libris Bibliotheca Tiliana (Plate, stamp and wax seal) = the extensive private library of the German entrepreneur, bibliophile and hunting scholar Kurt Lindner (1906-1987)

=260  \\$aHalle$bMajer$c1732
=300  \\$a[xxiv]-104 pages$bmusic examples, illustrations
=500  \\$aEngraved title page with organ, 4 putti playing instruments and singing, and various instruments hanging on the walls
=500  \\$aThe Music-Saal is in fact the second edition of Majer's Museum musicum theoretico practicum, published at Schwabisch Hall in 1732 and reprinted in 1954 as part of Barenreiter's 'Documenta musicologica' facsimile series, with a brief afterword by Heinz Becker
=500  \\$a Majer was organist and Kantor at St. Katharina, Schwabisch Hall, where he spent most of his life. The present work offers the earliest illustration and fingering instructions for the clarinet, which was not very widespread at the time.
